<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1316064257" /><table class="infobox vevent"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" class="infobox-above summary">Microsoft </td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="white-space: nowrap;"><a href="/wiki/Operating_system" title="Operating system">Operating system</a></th><td class="infobox-data"><a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">Android</a>, <a href="/wiki/IOS" title="IOS">iOS</a>, <a href="/wiki/Windows_10" title="Windows 10">Windows 10</a> and <a href="/wiki/Windows_11" title="Windows 11">11</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="white-space: nowrap;"><a href="/wiki/Software_categories#Categorization_approaches" title="Software categories">Type</a></th><td class="infobox-data"><a href="/wiki/Search_engine" title="Search engine">Search engine</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="white-space: nowrap;">Website</th><td class="infobox-data"><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.bing.com">www<wbr />.bing<wbr />.com</a></span>&#160;<span class="penicon autoconfirmed-show"><span class="mw-valign-text-top" typeof="mw:File/Frameless"><a href="https://www.wikidata.org/wiki/Q182496?uselang=en#P856" title="Edit this on Wikidata"><img alt="Edit this on Wikidata" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/8a/OOjs_UI_icon_edit-ltr-progressive.svg/20px-OOjs_UI_icon_edit-ltr-progressive.svg.png" decoding="async" width="10" height="10" class="mw-file-element" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a></span></span></td></tr></tbody></table> 
<p><b>Microsoft Bing</b> (also known simply as <b>Bing</b>) is a <a href="/wiki/Search_engine" title="Search engine">search engine</a> owned and operated by <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a>, and developed by <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_AI" title="Microsoft AI">Microsoft AI</a>. The service traces its roots back to Microsoft's earlier search engines, including <a href="/wiki/MSN_Search" class="mw-redirect" title="MSN Search">MSN Search</a>, <a href="/wiki/Windows_Live_Search" class="mw-redirect" title="Windows Live Search">Windows Live Search</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Live_Search" class="mw-redirect" title="Live Search">Live Search</a>. Bing offers a broad spectrum of search services, encompassing web, <a href="/wiki/Bing_Videos" title="Bing Videos">video</a>, image, and <a href="/wiki/Bing_Maps" title="Bing Maps">map search</a> products, all developed using <a href="/wiki/ASP.NET" title="ASP.NET">ASP.NET</a>.
</p><p>The transition from Live Search to Bing was announced by Microsoft CEO <a href="/wiki/Steve_Ballmer" title="Steve Ballmer">Steve Ballmer</a> on May 28, 2009, at the <i><a href="/wiki/All_Things_Digital" title="All Things Digital">All Things Digital</a></i> conference in <a href="/wiki/San_Diego" title="San Diego">San Diego</a>, California. The official release followed on June 3, 2009. Bing introduced several notable features at its inception, such as search suggestions during query input and a list of related searches, known as the 'Explore pane'. These features leveraged <a href="/wiki/Semantic_technology" title="Semantic technology">semantic technology</a> from <a href="/wiki/Powerset_(company)" title="Powerset (company)">Powerset</a>, a company Microsoft acquired in 2008. Microsoft also struck a deal with <a href="/wiki/Yahoo!" class="mw-redirect" title="Yahoo!">Yahoo!</a> that led to Bing powering <a href="/wiki/Yahoo!_Search" class="mw-redirect" title="Yahoo! Search">Yahoo! Search</a>.
</p><p>Microsoft made significant strides towards <a href="/wiki/Open-source_technology" class="mw-redirect" title="Open-source technology">open-source technology</a> in 2016, making the <a href="/wiki/BitFunnel" title="BitFunnel">BitFunnel</a> <a href="/wiki/Search_engine_indexing" title="Search engine indexing">search engine indexing</a> algorithm and various components of Bing open source. In February 2023, Microsoft launched Bing Chat (later renamed <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Copilot" title="Microsoft Copilot">Microsoft Copilot</a>), an <a href="/wiki/Artificial_intelligence" title="Artificial intelligence">artificial intelligence</a> <a href="/wiki/Chatbot" title="Chatbot">chatbot</a> experience based on <a href="/wiki/GPT-4" title="GPT-4">GPT-4</a>, integrated directly into the search engine. This was well-received, with Bing reaching 100 million active users by the following month. 
</p><p>As of April 2024, Bing holds the position of the second-largest search engine worldwide, with a market share of 3.64%, behind <a href="/wiki/Google_Search" title="Google Search">Google</a>'s 90.91%. Other competitors include <a href="/wiki/Yandex_Search" title="Yandex Search">Yandex</a> with 1.61%, <a href="/wiki/Baidu" title="Baidu">Baidu</a> with 1.15%, and <a href="/wiki/Yahoo" title="Yahoo">Yahoo!</a>, which is largely powered by Bing, with 1.13%.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Approximately 27.43% of Bing's monthly global traffic comes from <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>, 22.16% from the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, 4.85% from <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a>, 4.18% from <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a> and 3.61% from <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="History">History</h2></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Background_(1998–2009)"><span id="Background_.281998.E2.80.932009.29"></span>Background (1998–2009)</h3></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="MSN_Search">MSN Search</h4></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:MSN_Search_screenshot_2002.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/38/MSN_Search_screenshot_2002.png/250px-MSN_Search_screenshot_2002.png" decoding="async" width="250" height="283" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/3/38/MSN_Search_screenshot_2002.png 1.5x" data-file-width="262" data-file-height="297" /></a><figcaption>MSN Search homepage in 2002</figcaption></figure>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:MSN_Search_screenshot.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a3/MSN_Search_screenshot.png/250px-MSN_Search_screenshot.png" decoding="async" width="250" height="146" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/a/a3/MSN_Search_screenshot.png 1.5x" data-file-width="413" data-file-height="241" /></a><figcaption>MSN Search homepage in 2006</figcaption></figure>
<p>Microsoft launched <b>MSN Search</b> in the third quarter of 1998, using search results from <a href="/wiki/Inktomi" title="Inktomi">Inktomi</a>. It consisted of a search engine, index, and <a href="/wiki/Web_crawler" title="Web crawler">web crawler</a>. In early 1999, MSN Search launched a version which displayed listings from <a href="/wiki/Looksmart" class="mw-redirect" title="Looksmart">Looksmart</a> blended with results from Inktomi except for a short time in 1999 when results from <a href="/wiki/AltaVista" title="AltaVista">AltaVista</a> were used instead. Microsoft decided to make a large investment in web search by building its own <a href="/wiki/Web_crawler" title="Web crawler">web crawler</a> for MSN Search, the index of which was updated weekly and sometimes daily. The upgrade started as a <a href="/wiki/Beta_testing" class="mw-redirect" title="Beta testing">beta</a> program in November 2004, and came out of beta in February 2005.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This occurred a year after rival <a href="/wiki/Yahoo!_Search" class="mw-redirect" title="Yahoo! Search">Yahoo! Search</a> rolled out its own crawler. Image search was powered by a third party, <a href="/wiki/Picsearch" title="Picsearch">Picsearch</a>. The service also started providing its search results to other search engine portals in an effort to better compete in the market.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Windows_Live_Search">Windows Live Search</h4></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Windows_Live_Search_homepage_screenshot_(2006).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/7/70/Windows_Live_Search_homepage_screenshot_%282006%29.jpg/250px-Windows_Live_Search_homepage_screenshot_%282006%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="116" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/7/70/Windows_Live_Search_homepage_screenshot_%282006%29.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="464" data-file-height="215" /></a><figcaption>Windows Live Search homepage</figcaption></figure>
<p>The first public beta of <b>Windows Live Search</b> was unveiled on March 8, 2006, with the final release on September 11, 2006 replacing MSN Search. The new search engine used search tabs that include Web, news, images, music, desktop, local, and <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Encarta" class="mw-redirect" title="Microsoft Encarta">Microsoft Encarta</a>.
</p><p>In the roll-over from MSN Search to Windows Live Search, Microsoft stopped using Picsearch as their image search provider and started performing their own image search, fueled by their own internal image search algorithms.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Live_Search">Live Search</h4></div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1320445320">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}@media print{body.ns-0 .mw-parser-output .hatnote{display:none!important}}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">"Live Search" redirects here. For other uses, see <a href="/wiki/Incremental_search" title="Incremental search">Incremental search</a>.</div>
<figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Live_Search_New.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/23/Live_Search_New.png/250px-Live_Search_New.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="128" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/23/Live_Search_New.png/330px-Live_Search_New.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/2/23/Live_Search_New.png 2x" data-file-width="413" data-file-height="241" /></a><figcaption>Live Search homepage, which would help to create the Bing homepage later on</figcaption></figure>
<p>On March 21, 2007, Microsoft announced that it would separate its search developments from the <a href="/wiki/Windows_Live" title="Windows Live">Windows Live</a> services family, rebranding the service as <b>Live Search</b>. Live Search was integrated into the <i>Live Search and Ad Platform</i> headed by <a href="/wiki/Satya_Nadella" title="Satya Nadella">Satya Nadella</a>, part of Microsoft's Platform and Systems division. As part of this change, Live Search was merged with <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_adCenter" class="mw-redirect" title="Microsoft adCenter">Microsoft adCenter</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>A series of reorganizations and consolidations of Microsoft's search offerings were made under the Live Search branding. On May 23, 2008, Microsoft discontinued <a href="/wiki/Live_Search_Books" title="Live Search Books">Live Search Books</a> and <a href="/wiki/Live_Search_Academic" title="Live Search Academic">Live Search Academic</a> and integrated all academic and book search results into regular search. This also included the closure of the <a href="/wiki/Live_Search_Books_Publisher_Program" class="mw-redirect" title="Live Search Books Publisher Program">Live Search Books Publisher Program</a>. <a href="/wiki/Windows_Live_Expo" title="Windows Live Expo">Windows Live Expo</a> was discontinued on July 31, 2008. Live Search Macros, a service for users to create their own custom search engines or use macros created by other users, was also discontinued. On May 15, 2009, <a href="/wiki/Live_Product_Upload" class="mw-redirect" title="Live Product Upload">Live Product Upload</a>, a service which allowed merchants to upload products information onto <a href="/wiki/Live_Search_Products" class="mw-redirect" title="Live Search Products">Live Search Products</a>, was discontinued. The final reorganization came as <a href="/wiki/Live_Search_QnA" class="mw-redirect" title="Live Search QnA">Live Search QnA</a> was rebranded <a href="/wiki/MSN_QnA" title="MSN QnA">MSN QnA</a> on February 18, 2009, then discontinued on May 21, 2009.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Beginnings_(2009)"><span id="Beginnings_.282009.29"></span>Beginnings (2009)</h3></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Rebrand_as_Bing">Rebrand as Bing</h4></div>

class="thumbcaption">Fourth <a href="/wiki/Fluent_Design_System" title="Fluent Design System">Fluent</a> Bing logo, used since 2020</div></div></div></div></div>
<p>Microsoft recognized that there would be a problem with branding as long as the word "Live" remained in the name.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> As an effort to create a new identity for Microsoft's search services, Live Search was officially replaced by Bing on June 3, 2009.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The Bing name was chosen through focus groups, and Microsoft decided that the name was memorable, short, and easy to spell, and that it would function well as a URL around the world. The word would remind people of the sound made during "the moment of discovery and decision making".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Microsoft was assisted by branding consultancy Interbrand in finding the new name.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The name also has strong similarity to the word <i><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/bingo" class="extiw" title="wikt:bingo">bingo</a></i>, which means that something sought has been found, as called out when winning the game <a href="/wiki/Bingo_(U.S.)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bingo (U.S.)">Bingo</a>. Microsoft advertising strategist David Webster proposed the name "Bang" for the same reasons the name Bing was ultimately chosen (easy to spell, one syllable, and easy to remember). He noted, "It's there, it's an exclamation point [...] It's the opposite of a question mark." <i>Bang</i> was ultimately not chosen because it could not be properly used as a verb in the context of an internet search; Webster commented "Oh, 'I banged it' is very different than &#32;&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Sic" title="Sic">sic</a></i>&#93; 'I binged it'".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Qi Lu, president of Microsoft Online Services, also announced that Bing's official Chinese name is <i>bì yìng</i> (<a href="/wiki/Simplified_Chinese_characters" title="Simplified Chinese characters">simplified Chinese</a>&#58; <span lang="zh-Hans">必应</span>; <a href="/wiki/Traditional_Chinese_characters" title="Traditional Chinese characters">traditional Chinese</a>&#58; <span lang="zh-Hant">必應</span>), which literally means "very certain to respond" or "very certain to answer" in Chinese.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>While being tested internally by Microsoft employees, Bing's codename was <i><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/en:kumo#Japanese" class="extiw" title="wikt:en:kumo">Kumo</a></i> (<a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/en:%E3%81%8F%E3%82%82#Japanese" class="extiw" title="wikt:en:くも">くも</a>),<sup id="cite&#95;ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> which came from the <a href="/wiki/Japanese_language" title="Japanese language">Japanese</a> word for <i><a href="/wiki/Spider" title="Spider">spider</a></i> (<a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/en:%E8%9C%98%E8%9B%9B#Japanese" class="extiw" title="wikt:en:蜘蛛">蜘蛛</a>; <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/en:%E3%81%8F%E3%82%82#Japanese" class="extiw" title="wikt:en:くも">くも</a>, <i><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/en:kumo#Japanese" class="extiw" title="wikt:en:kumo">kumo</a></i>) as well as <i><a href="/wiki/Cloud" title="Cloud">cloud</a></i> (<a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/en:%E9%9B%B2#Japanese" class="extiw" title="wikt:en:雲">雲</a>; <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/en:%E3%81%8F%E3%82%82#Japanese" class="extiw" title="wikt:en:くも">くも</a>, <i><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/en:kumo#Japanese" class="extiw" title="wikt:en:kumo">kumo</a></i>), referring to the manner in which search engines "<a href="/wiki/Web_crawler" title="Web crawler">spider</a>" Internet resources to add them to their database, as well as <a href="/wiki/Cloud_computing" title="Cloud computing">cloud computing</a>.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Deal_with_Yahoo!"><span id="Deal_with_Yahoo.21"></span>Deal with Yahoo!</h4></div>
<p>On July 29, 2009, Microsoft and <a href="/wiki/Yahoo!" class="mw-redirect" title="Yahoo!">Yahoo!</a> announced that they had made a ten-year deal in which the Yahoo! <a href="/wiki/Search_engine" title="Search engine">search engine</a> would be replaced by Bing, retaining the Yahoo! <a href="/wiki/User_interface" title="User interface">user interface</a>. Yahoo! got to keep 88% of the revenue from all search ad sales on its site for the first five years of the deal, and have the right to sell advertising on some <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a> sites.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> All Yahoo! Search global customers and partners made the transition by early 2012.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-YahooHelp&#95;22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-YahooHelp-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Legal_challenges">Legal challenges</h4></div>
<p>On July 31, 2009, The Laptop Company, Inc. stated in a press release that it would challenge Bing's trademark application, alleging that Bing may cause confusion in the marketplace as Bing and their product BongoBing both do online product search.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Software company TeraByte Unlimited, which has a product called BootIt Next Generation (abbreviated to BING), also contended the trademark application on similar grounds, as did a Missouri-based design company called Bing! Information Design.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Guardian&#95;24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian-24"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Microsoft contended that claims challenging its trademark were without merit because these companies filed for U.S. federal trademark applications only after Microsoft filed for the Bing trademark in March 2009.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Growth_(2009–2023)"><span id="Growth_.282009.E2.80.932023.29"></span>Growth (2009–2023)</h3></div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1305433154">.mw-parser-output .ambox{border:1px solid #a2a9b1;border-left:10px solid #36c;background-color:#fbfbfb;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .ambox-move{border-left:10px solid #9932cc}.mw-parser-output .ambox-protection{border-left:10px solid #a2a9b1}.mw-parser-output .ambox .mbox-text{border:none;padding:0.25em
