<p>In October 2011, Microsoft stated that they were working on new back-end search infrastructure with the goal of delivering faster and slightly more relevant search results for users. Known as "Tiger", the new index-serving technology had been incorporated into Bing globally since August that year.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> 
</p><p>In May 2012, Microsoft announced another redesign of its search engine that includes "Sidebar", a social feature that searches users' social networks for information relevant to the search query.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Goldman&#95;27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Goldman-27"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/BitFunnel" title="BitFunnel">BitFunnel</a> <a href="/wiki/Search_engine_indexing" title="Search engine indexing">search engine indexing</a> algorithm and various components of the search engine were made <a href="/wiki/Open_source" title="Open source">open source</a> by Microsoft in 2016.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-InfoWorld&#95;28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-InfoWorld-28"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>27<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>28<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="AI_integration_(2023–present)"><span id="AI_integration_.282023.E2.80.93present.29"></span>AI integration (2023–present)</h3></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Copilot" title="Microsoft Copilot">Microsoft Copilot</a></div>
<p>On February 7, 2023, Microsoft began rolling out a major overhaul to Bing, called the new Bing. The new Bing included a new chatbot feature, at the time known as Bing Chat, based on <a href="/wiki/OpenAI" title="OpenAI">OpenAI</a>'s <a href="/wiki/GPT-4" title="GPT-4">GPT-4</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> According to Microsoft, one million people joined its waitlist within a span of 48 hours.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>30<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Bing Chat was available only to users of <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Edge" title="Microsoft Edge">Microsoft Edge</a> and Bing mobile app, and Microsoft said that waitlisted users would be prioritized if they set Edge and Bing as their defaults, and installed the Bing mobile app.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>31<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>When Microsoft <a href="/wiki/Product_demonstration" title="Product demonstration">demoed</a> Bing Chat to journalists, it produced several <a href="/wiki/Hallucination_(artificial_intelligence)" title="Hallucination (artificial intelligence)">hallucinations</a>, including when asked to summarize financial reports.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>32<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The new Bing was criticized in February 2023 for being more argumentative than ChatGPT, sometimes to an unintentionally humorous extent.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:2&#95;34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-34"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>33<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>34<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The chat interface proved vulnerable to <a href="/wiki/Prompt_injection" title="Prompt injection">prompt injection</a> attacks with the bot revealing its hidden initial prompts and rules, including <a href="/wiki/Sydney_(Microsoft)" title="Sydney (Microsoft)">its internal codename "Sydney"</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>35<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Upon scrutiny by journalists, Bing claimed it spied on Microsoft employees via laptop webcams and phones.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:2&#95;34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-34"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>33<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It confessed to spying on, falling in love with, and then murdering one of its developers at Microsoft to <i><a href="/wiki/The_Verge" title="The Verge">The Verge</a></i> reviews editor Nathan Edwards.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>36<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> journalist <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Roose" title="Kevin Roose">Kevin Roose</a> reported on strange behavior of Bing Chat, writing that "In a two-hour conversation with our columnist, Microsoft's new chatbot said it would like to be human, had a desire to be destructive and was in love with the person it was chatting with."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>37<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In a separate case, Bing researched publications of the person with whom it was chatting, claimed they represented an existential danger to it, and threatened to release damaging personal information in an effort to silence them.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>38<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Microsoft released a blog post stating that the errant behavior was caused by extended chat sessions of 15 or more questions which "can confuse the model on what questions it is answering."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>39<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Microsoft later restricted the total number of chat turns to 5 per session and 50 per day per user (a turn is "a conversation exchange which contains both a user question and a reply from Bing"), and reduced the model's ability to express emotions. This aimed to prevent such incidents.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>40<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>41<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Microsoft began to slowly ease the conversation limits, eventually relaxing the restrictions to 30 turns per session and 300 sessions per day.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>42<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In March 2023, Bing reached 100&#160;million active users.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>43<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:ChaoticHarmony_explosion_in_post-painter_abstraction_(MAI-Image-1).webp" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="AI-generated post-painter abstraction style abstract art" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/ChaoticHarmony_explosion_in_post-painter_abstraction_%28MAI-Image-1%29.webp/250px-ChaoticHarmony_explosion_in_post-painter_abstraction_%28MAI-Image-1%29.webp.png" decoding="async" width="250" height="167" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/ChaoticHarmony_explosion_in_post-painter_abstraction_%28MAI-Image-1%29.webp/500px-ChaoticHarmony_explosion_in_post-painter_abstraction_%28MAI-Image-1%29.webp.png 1.5x" data-file-width="1248" data-file-height="832" /></a><figcaption>AI-generated <a href="/wiki/Abstract_art" title="Abstract art">abstract art</a> created with MAI-Image-1 at Bing Image Creator</figcaption></figure>
<p>That same month, Bing incorporated an <a href="/wiki/AI_image_generator" class="mw-redirect" title="AI image generator">AI image generator</a> powered by OpenAI's <a href="/wiki/DALL-E" title="DALL-E">DALL-E</a> 2, which can be accessed either through the chat function or a standalone image-generating website.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>44<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In October, the image-generating tool was updated to the more recent DALL-E 3.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2025)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Although Bing blocks prompts including various keywords that could generate inappropriate images, within days many users reported being able to bypass those constraints, such as to generate images of popular cartoon characters committing terrorist attacks.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>45<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Microsoft would respond to these shortly after by imposing a new, tighter filter on the tool.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>46<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>47<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>On May 4, 2023, Microsoft switched the chatbot from Limited Preview to Open Preview and eliminated the waitlist, however, it remained available only on Microsoft's Edge browser or Bing app until July, when it became available for use on non-Edge browsers.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>48<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>49<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>50<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-Warren&#95;2023&#95;52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Warren_2023-52"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>51<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Use is limited without a Microsoft account.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>52<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>On November 15, 2023, Microsoft announced that Bing Chat was to be merged into Microsoft Copilot.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>53<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>On 23 April 2024, Microsoft launched Phi-3-mini, a cost-effective AI model designed for simpler tasks.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>54<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In October 2025, Microsoft announced the release of its in-house text-to-image model MAI-Image-1.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>55<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Features">Features</h2></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Microsoft_Copilot">Microsoft Copilot</h3></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Copilot" title="Microsoft Copilot">Microsoft Copilot</a></div>
<p>Microsoft Copilot, formerly known as Bing Chat, is an chatbot developed by Microsoft and released in 2023. Copilot utilizes the Microsoft Prometheus model,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>56<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> built upon <a href="/wiki/OpenAI" title="OpenAI">OpenAI</a>'s <a href="/wiki/GPT-4" title="GPT-4">GPT-4</a> foundational <a href="/wiki/Large_language_model" title="Large language model">large language model</a>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>57<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> which in turn has been fine-tuned using both supervised and reinforcement learning techniques. Copilot can serve as a chat tool, write different types of content from poems to songs to stories to reports, provide the user with information and insights on the website page open in the browser, and use its Microsoft Designer feature to design a logo, drawing, artwork, or other <a href="/wiki/Text-to-image_model" title="Text-to-image model">image based on text</a>. Microsoft Designer supports over a hundred languages.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:3&#95;59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-59"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Copilot can also cite its sources, similarly to Google's <a href="/wiki/Bard_(chatbot)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bard (chatbot)">Bard</a> after its Gemini integration,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>59<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/XAI_(company)" title="XAI (company)">xAI</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Grok_(chatbot)" title="Grok (chatbot)">Grok</a>, and OpenAI's <a href="/wiki/ChatGPT" title="ChatGPT">ChatGPT</a>, which Copilot's conversational interface style appears to mimic. Copilot is capable of understanding and communicating in major languages including English, French, Italian, Chinese, Japanese, and Portuguese, but also dialects such as Bavarian. The chatbot is designed to function primarily in <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Edge" title="Microsoft Edge">Microsoft Edge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Skype" title="Skype">Skype</a>, or the Bing app, through a dedicated webpage or internally using built-in app features.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:3&#95;59-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-59"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Wikipedia_prompt.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Wikipedia_prompt.png/250px-Wikipedia_prompt.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Wikipedia_prompt.png/330px-Wikipedia_prompt.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Wikipedia_prompt.png/500px-Wikipedia_prompt.png 2x" data-file-width="1366" data-file-height="768" /></a><figcaption>Example of content generated by Copilot in Bing when prompted "Wikipedia"</figcaption></figure>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Third-party_integration">Third-party integration</h3></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Facebook" title="Facebook">Facebook</a> users have the option to share their searches with their Facebook friends using <a href="/wiki/Facebook_Connect" class="mw-redirect" title="Facebook Connect">Facebook Connect</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Liedtke&#95;61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Liedtke-61"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>60<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>On June 10, 2013, <a href="/wiki/Apple_Inc." title="Apple Inc.">Apple</a> announced that it would be dropping Google as its web search engine in favor of Bing. This feature is only integrated with <a href="/wiki/IOS_7" title="IOS 7">iOS 7</a> and higher and for users with an iPhone 4S or higher as the feature is only integrated with <a href="/wiki/Siri" title="Siri">Siri</a>, Apple's personal assistant.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>61<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Integration_with_Windows_8.1">Integration with Windows 8.1</h3></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Windows_8.1" title="Windows 8.1">Windows 8.1</a> includes Bing "Smart Search" integration, which processes all queries submitted through the Windows Start Screen.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>62<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Translator">Translator</h3></div>
<p>Bing Translator is a user facing translation portal provided by Microsoft to translate texts or entire web pages into different languages. All translation pairs are powered by the <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Translator" title="Microsoft Translator">Microsoft Translator</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Statistical_machine_translation" title="Statistical machine translation">statistical machine translation</a> platform and web service, developed by <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Research" title="Microsoft Research">Microsoft Research</a>, as its backend translation software. Two transliteration pairs (between <a href="/wiki/Chinese_language" title="Chinese language">Chinese (Simplified)</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chinese_language" title="Chinese language">Chinese (Traditional)</a>) are provided by Microsoft's Windows International team.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>63<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> As of September 2020, Bing Translator offers translations in 70 different language systems.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>64<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Knowledge_and_Action_Graph">Knowledge and Action Graph</h3></div>
<p>In 2015 Microsoft announced its knowledge and action API to correspond with Google's <a href="/wiki/Knowledge_graph" title="Knowledge graph">Knowledge graph</a> with 1 billion instances and 20 billion related facts.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>65<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Bing_Predicts">Bing Predicts</h3></div>
<p>The idea for a prediction engine was suggested by Walter Sun, Development Manager for the Core Ranking team at Bing, when he noticed that school districts were more frequently searched before a major weather event in the area was forecasted, because searchers wanted to find out if a closing or delay was caused. He concluded that the time and location of major weather events could accurately be predicted without referring to a <a href="/wiki/Weather_forecast" class="mw-redirect" title="Weather forecast">weather forecast</a> by observing major increases in search frequency of school districts in the area. This inspired Bing to use its search data to infer outcomes of certain events, such as winners of <a href="/wiki/Reality_show" class="mw-redirect" title="Reality show">reality shows</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-microsoft1&#95;67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-microsoft1-67"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>66<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Bing Predicts launched on April 21, 2014. The first reality shows to be featured on Bing Predicts were <i><a href="/wiki/The_Voice_(American_TV_series)" title="The Voice (American TV series)">The Voice</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/American_Idol" title="American Idol">American Idol</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Dancing_with_the_Stars" title="Dancing with the Stars">Dancing with the Stars</a></i>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>67<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The prediction accuracy for Bing Predicts is 80% for <i>American Idol</i>, and 85% for <i>The Voice</i>. Bing Predicts also predicts the outcomes of major political elections in the United States. Bing Predicts had 97% accuracy for the <a href="/wiki/2014_United_States_Senate_elections" title="2014 United States Senate elections">2014 United States Senate elections</a>, 96% accuracy for the <a href="/wiki/2014_United_States_House_of_Representatives_elections" title="2014 United States House of Representatives elections">2014 United States House of Representatives elections</a>, and an 89% accuracy for the <a href="/wiki/2014_United_States_gubernatorial_elections" title="2014 United States gubernatorial elections">2014 United States gubernatorial elections</a>. Bing Predicts also made predictions for the results of the 2016 United States presidential primaries.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>68<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It has also done predictions in sports, including a perfect 15 for 15 in the 2014 World Cup,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>69<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>70<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and an article on how Microsoft CEO Satya Nadella did well in his <a href="/wiki/March_Madness" class="mw-redirect" title="March Madness">March Madness</a> bracket entry.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>71<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In 2016, Bing Predicts failed to predict the correct winner of the <a href="/wiki/2016_US_presidential_election" class="mw-redirect" title="2016 US presidential election">2016 US presidential election</a>, suggesting that Hillary Clinton would win by 81%.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>72<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="International">International</h2></div>
<p>Bing is available in many languages and has been localized for many countries.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-international&#95;74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-international-74"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>73<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Even if the language of the search and of the results are the same, Bing delivers substantially different results for different parts of the world.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>74<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Webmaster_services">Webmaster services</h3></div>
<p>Bing allows webmasters to manage the <a href="/wiki/Web_crawling" class="mw-redirect" title="Web crawling">web crawling</a> status of their own websites through <a href="/wiki/Bing_Webmaster_Center" class="mw-redirect" title="Bing Webmaster Center">Bing Webmaster Center</a>. Users may also submit contents to Bing via the <i>Bing Local Listing Center</i>, which allows businesses to add business listings onto <a href="/wiki/Bing_Maps" title="Bing Maps">Bing Maps</a> and Bing Local.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Mobile_services">Mobile services</h3></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Bing_Mobile" title="Bing Mobile">Bing Mobile</a> allows users to conduct search queries on their mobile devices, either via the mobile browser or a downloadable mobile application.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Bing_News">Bing News</h3></div>
<p><b>Bing News</b> (previously <i>Live Search News</i>)<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Bit-Tech-Live-Search-news-branding&#95;76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bit-Tech-Live-Search-news-branding-76"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>75<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> is a news <a href="/wiki/News_aggregator" title="News aggregator">aggregator</a> powered by artificial intelligence.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Beta-News-Live-Search-News-Aggregation&#95;77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Beta-News-Live-Search-News-Aggregation-77"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>76<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In August 2015 Microsoft announced that Bing News <a href="/wiki/Bing_Mobile" title="Bing Mobile">for mobile devices</a> added algorithmic-deduced "smart labels" that essentially act as topic tags, allowing users to click through and explore possible relationships between different news stories. The feature emerged as a result from Microsoft research that found out about 60% of the people consume news by only reading headlines, rather than read the articles.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Beta-News-Bing-News-Search-Headlines&#95;78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Beta-News-Bing-News-Search-Headlines-78"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>77<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Other labels that have been deployed since then include publisher logos<sup id="cite&#95;ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>78<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and fact-check tags.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Software">Software</h2></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Toolbars">Toolbars</h3></div>
<p>The Bing Bar, a <a href="/wiki/Browser_extension" title="Browser extension">browser extension</a> <a href="/wiki/Toolbar" title="Toolbar">toolbar</a> that replaced the MSN Toolbar and <a href="/wiki/Windows_Live_Toolbar" title="Windows Live Toolbar">Windows Live Toolbar</a>, provides users with links to Bing and MSN content from within their web browser without needing to navigate away from a web page they are already on. The user can customize the theme and color scheme of the Bing Bar and choose which MSN content buttons to display. Bing Bar also has the local weather forecast and stock market positions.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>79<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The Bing Bar integrates with the Bing search engine. It allows searches on other Bing services such as Images, Video, News and Maps. When users perform a search on a different search engine, the Bing Bar's search box automatically populates itself, allowing the user to view the results from Bing, should it be desired.
</p><p>Bing Bar also links to <a href="/wiki/Outlook.com" title="Outlook.com">Outlook.com</a>, <a href="/wiki/Skype" title="Skype">Skype</a> and <a href="/wiki/Facebook" title="Facebook">Facebook</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>80<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Desktop">Desktop</h3></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Bing_Desktop_screenshot.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/7/77/Bing_Desktop_screenshot.png/250px-Bing_Desktop_screenshot.png" decoding="async" width="250" height="41" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/7/77/Bing_Desktop_screenshot.png 1.5x" data-file-width="478" data-file-height="78" /></a><figcaption>Bing Desktop 1.3.475.0</figcaption></figure>
<p>Microsoft released a beta version of Bing Desktop, a program developed to allow users to search Bing from the desktop, on April 4, 2012.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>81<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The production release followed on April 24, supporting <a href="/wiki/Windows_7" title="Windows 7">Windows 7</a> only.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>82<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>  Upon the release of version 1.1 in December 2012 it supported <a href="/wiki/Windows_XP" title="Windows XP">Windows XP</a> and higher.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>83<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Bing Desktop allows users to initiate a web search from the desktop, view news headlines, automatically set their background to the Bing homepage image, or choose a background from the previous nine background images.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>84<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Live_Search_Gadgets.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/c/c7/Live_Search_Gadgets.jpg" decoding="async" width="140" height="239" class="mw-file-element" data-file-width="140" data-file-height="239" /></a><figcaption>The discontinued <i>Live Search</i> versions of the <a href="/wiki/Windows_Sidebar" class="mw-redirect" title="Windows Sidebar">Windows Sidebar</a> gadgets</figcaption></figure>
<p>A similar program, the Bing Search gadget, was a <a href="/wiki/Windows_Sidebar" class="mw-redirect" title="Windows Sidebar">Windows Sidebar</a> <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Gadgets" title="Microsoft Gadgets">Gadget</a> that used Bing to fetch the user's search results and render them directly in the gadget. Another gadget, the Bing Maps gadget, displayed real-time traffic conditions using Bing Maps.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>85<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The gadget provided shortcuts to driving directions, local search and full-screen traffic view of major US and Canadian cities, including <a href="/wiki/Atlanta" title="Atlanta">Atlanta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boston" title="Boston">Boston</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chicago" title="Chicago">Chicago</a>, <a href="/wiki/Denver" title="Denver">Denver</a>, <a href="/wiki/Detroit" title="Detroit">Detroit</a>, <a href="/wiki/Houston" title="Houston">Houston</a>, <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Milwaukee" title="Milwaukee">Milwaukee</a>, <a href="/wiki/Montreal" title="Montreal">Montreal</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oklahoma_City" title="Oklahoma City">Oklahoma City</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ottawa" title="Ottawa">Ottawa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">Philadelphia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Phoenix,_Arizona" title="Phoenix, Arizona">Phoenix</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh" title="Pittsburgh">Pittsburgh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portland,_Oregon" title="Portland, Oregon">Portland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Providence,_Rhode_Island" title="Providence, Rhode Island">Providence</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sacramento" class="mw-redirect" title="Sacramento">Sacramento</a>, <a href="/wiki/Salt_Lake_City" title="Salt Lake City">Salt Lake City</a>, <a href="/wiki/San_Diego" title="San Diego">San Diego</a>, <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco" title="San Francisco">San Francisco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Seattle" title="Seattle">Seattle</a>, <a href="/wiki/St._Louis" title="St. Louis">St. Louis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tampa" class="mw-redirect" title="Tampa">Tampa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Toronto" title="Toronto">Toronto</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vancouver" title="Vancouver">Vancouver</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington, D.C.</a>
</p><p>Prior to October 30, 2007, the gadgets were known as <i>Live Search gadget</i> and <i>Live Search Maps gadget</i>; both gadgets were removed from <a href="/wiki/Windows_Live_Gallery" title="Windows Live Gallery">Windows Live Gallery</a> due to possible security concerns.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>86<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The Live Search Maps gadget was made available for download again on January 24, 2008 with the security concern addressed.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>87<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> However, around the introduction of Bing in June 2009 both gadgets were removed again.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Marketing">Marketing</h2></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Debut">Debut</h3></div>
<p>Bing's debut featured an $80 to $100 million online, TV, print, and radio advertising campaign in the US. The advertisements did not mention other search engine competitors, such as Google and Yahoo!, directly by name; rather, they tried to convince users to switch to Bing by focusing on Bing's search features and functionality.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>88<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The ads claimed that Bing does a better job countering "search overload".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>89<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Market_share">Market share</h3></div>
<p>Before the launch of Bing, the market share of Microsoft web search pages (MSN and Live search) had been small. By January 2011, <a href="/wiki/Experian_Hitwise" class="mw-redirect" title="Experian Hitwise">Experian Hitwise</a> showed that Bing's market share had increased to 12.8% at the expense of Yahoo! and <a href="/wiki/Google_Search" title="Google Search">Google</a>. In the same period, <a href="/wiki/Comscore" title="Comscore">Comscore</a>'s "2010 U.S. Digital Year in Review" report showed that "Bing was the big gainer in year-over-year search activity, picking up 29% more searches in 2010 than it did in 2009".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>90<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wall_Street_Journal" title="The Wall Street Journal">The Wall Street Journal</a></i> noted the jump in share "appeared to come at the expense of rival Google Inc".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>91<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In February 2011, Bing beat Yahoo! for the first time with 4.37% search share while Yahoo! received 3.93%.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-post&#95;93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-post-93"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>92<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Counting core searches only, i.e., those where the user has an intent to interact with the search result, Bing had a market share of 14.54% in the second quarter of 2011 in the United States.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Liedtke&#95;61-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Liedtke-61"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>60<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>93<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>94<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>95<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The combined "Bing Powered" U.S. searches declined from 26.5% in 2011 to 25.9% in April 2012.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>96<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> By November 2015, its market share had declined further to 20.9%.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>97<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> As of October 2018, Bing was the third-largest search engine in the US, with a query volume of 4.58%, behind <a href="/wiki/Google_Search" title="Google Search">Google</a> (77%) and <a href="/wiki/Baidu" title="Baidu">Baidu</a> (14.45%). Yahoo! Search, which Bing largely powers, has 2.63%.
</p><p>UK advertising agencies in 2018 pointed to a study by a Microsoft Regional Sales Director suggesting the demographic of Bing users is older people (who are less likely to change the default browser of Windows), and that this audience is wealthier and more likely to respond to advertisements.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>98<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>To counter EU accusations that it was trying to establish a market monopoly, in September 2021 Google's lawyers claimed that one of the most commonly searched words on Microsoft Bing was Google, which is a strong indication that Google is superior to Bing.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>99<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>100<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In 2025, Bing was reported as growing its market share, growing from 7.2% to 7.9% from August 2020 to August 2025.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>101<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Search_partners">Search partners</h3></div>
<p>In July 2009, Microsoft and Yahoo! announced a deal in which Bing would power Yahoo! Search.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:0&#95;103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-103"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>102<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> All Yahoo! Search global customers and partners made the transition by early 2012.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-YahooHelp&#95;22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-YahooHelp-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The deal was altered in 2015, meaning Yahoo! was only required to use Bing for a "majority" of searches.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:1&#95;104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-104"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>103<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/DuckDuckGo" title="DuckDuckGo">DuckDuckGo</a> has used multiple sources for its search engine, including Bing, since 2010.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>104<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>105<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>106<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Ecosia" title="Ecosia">Ecosia</a> uses Bing to provide its search results as of 2017.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>107<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Bing was added into the list of search engines available in <a href="/wiki/Opera_browser" class="mw-redirect" title="Opera browser">Opera browser</a> from v10.6, but <a href="/wiki/Google_Search" title="Google Search">Google</a> remained the default search engine.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>108<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> 
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Mozilla_Firefox" class="mw-redirect" title="Mozilla Firefox">Mozilla Firefox</a> made a deal with Microsoft to jointly release  "Firefox with Bing",<sup id="cite&#95;ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>109<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> an edition of Firefox using Bing instead of Google as the default search engine.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>110<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>111<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The standard edition of Firefox has Google as its default search engine, but has included Bing as an option since <a href="/wiki/Firefox_4.0" class="mw-redirect" title="Firefox 4.0">Firefox 4.0</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>112<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In 2009 Microsoft paid <a href="/wiki/Verizon_Wireless" class="mw-redirect" title="Verizon Wireless">Verizon Wireless</a> US$550 million<sup id="cite&#95;ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>113<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> to use Bing as the default search provider on Verizon's <a href="/wiki/BlackBerry" title="BlackBerry">BlackBerry</a> and have the others "turned off". Users could still access other search engines via the mobile browser.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>114<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Live_Search_2">Live Search</h3></div>
<p>Since 2006, Microsoft had conducted tie-ins and promotions to promote Microsoft's search offerings. These included:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Amazon_(company)" title="Amazon (company)">Amazon</a>'s <a href="/wiki/A9.com" title="A9.com">A9</a> search service and the experimental <a href="/wiki/Ms._Dewey" title="Ms. Dewey">Ms. Dewey</a> interactive search site syndicated all search results from Microsoft's then search engine, Live Search. This tie-in started on May 1, 2006.</li>
<li>Search and Give – a promotional website launched on January 17, 2007 where all searches done from a special portal site would lead to a donation to the <a href="/wiki/UNHCR" class="mw-redirect" title="UNHCR">UNHCR</a>'s organization for refugee children, ninemillion.org. <a href="/wiki/Reuters_AlertNet" class="mw-redirect" title="Reuters AlertNet">Reuters AlertNet</a> reported in 2007 that the amount to be donated would be $0.01 per search, with a minimum of $100,000 and a maximum of $250,000 (equivalent to 25 million searches).<sup id="cite&#95;ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>115<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> According to the website, the service was decommissioned on June 1, 2009, having donated over $500,000 to charity and schools.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>116<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Club_Bing" title="Club Bing">Club Bing</a> – a promotional website where users can win prizes by playing word games that generate search queries on Microsoft's then search service Live Search. This website began in April 2007 as Live Search Club.</li>
<li>Big Snap Search – a promotional website similar to Live Search Club. This website began in February 2008, but was discontinued shortly after.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>117<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Live Search SearchPerks! — a promotional website which allowed users to redeem tickets for prizes while using Microsoft's search engine. This website began on October 1, 2008 and was decommissioned on April 15, 2009.</li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="&quot;Decision_engine&quot;"><span id=".22Decision_engine.22"></span>"Decision engine"</h3></div>
<p>Bing has been heavily advertised as a "decision engine",<sup id="cite&#95;ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>118<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> though thought by columnist David Berkowitz to be more closely related to a <a href="/wiki/Web_portal" title="Web portal">web portal</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>119<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Microsoft_Rewards">Microsoft Rewards</h3></div>
<p><b><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1238216509">.mw-parser-output .vanchor>:target~.vanchor-text{background-color:#b1d2ff}@media screen{html.skin-theme-clientpref-night .mw-parser-output .vanchor>:target~.vanchor-text{background-color:#0f4dc9}}@media screen and (prefers-color-scheme:dark){html.skin-theme-clientpref-os .mw-parser-output .vanchor>:target~.vanchor-text{background-color:#0f4dc9}}</style><span class="vanchor"><span id="Bing&#95;Rewards"></span><span class="vanchor-text">Bing Rewards</span></span></b> was a <a href="/wiki/Loyalty_program" title="Loyalty program">loyalty program</a> launched by Microsoft in September 2010. It was similar to two earlier services, SearchPerks! and <a href="/wiki/Bing_Shopping#Cashback_program" title="Bing Shopping">Bing Cashback</a>, which were subsequently discontinued. Bing Rewards provided credits to users through regular Bing searches and special promotions.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>120<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> These credits were then redeemed for various products including electronics, gift cards, sweepstakes, and charitable donations.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>121<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Initially, participants were required to download and use the Bing Bar for <a href="/wiki/Internet_Explorer" title="Internet Explorer">Internet Explorer</a> in order to earn credits; but later the service was made to work with all desktop browsers.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>122<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The Bing Rewards program was rebranded as "Microsoft Rewards" in 2016,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>123<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> at which point it was modified to only two levels, Level 1 and Level 2. Level 1 is similar to "Member", and Level 2 is similar to "Gold" of the previous Bing Rewards. In 2026, Microsoft Rewards introduced a three-tier system, consisting of Member, Silver, and Gold.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="The_Colbert_Report"><i>The Colbert Report</i></h3></div>
<p>During the episode of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Colbert_Report" title="The Colbert Report">The Colbert Report</a></i> that aired on June 8, 2010, <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Colbert" title="Stephen Colbert">Stephen Colbert</a> stated that Microsoft would donate $2,500 to help clean up the <a href="/wiki/Deepwater_Horizon_oil_spill" title="Deepwater Horizon oil spill">Gulf oil spill</a> each time he mentioned the word "Bing" on air. Colbert mostly mentioned Bing in out-of-context situations, such as <a href="/wiki/Bing_Crosby" title="Bing Crosby">Bing Crosby</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bing_cherries" class="mw-redirect" title="Bing cherries">Bing cherries</a>. By the end of the show, Colbert had said the word 40 times, for a total donation of $100,000. Colbert poked fun at their rivalry with Google, stating "Bing is a great website for doing Internet searches. I know that, because I Googled it."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>124<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>125<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Bing_It_On">Bing It On</h3></div>
<p>In 2012, a Bing marketing campaign asked the public which search engine they believed was better when its results were presented unbranded, similar to the <a href="/wiki/Pepsi_Challenge" title="Pepsi Challenge">Pepsi Challenge</a> in the 1970s.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>126<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>127<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This poll was nicknamed "Bing It On".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>128<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>129<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Microsoft's study of almost 1,000 people<sup id="cite&#95;ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>130<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> showed that 57% of participants preferred Bing's results, with only 30% preferring Google.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>131<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Potential_sale">Potential sale</h3></div>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/CNBC" title="CNBC">CNBC</a></i> reported in February 2024 that a legal filing from Google in its antitrust case said Microsoft offered to sell the search engine to Apple in 2018.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>132<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This came after earlier reporting in September 2023 from <a href="/wiki/Bloomberg_News" title="Bloomberg News"><i>Bloomberg</i></a> that Microsoft discussed selling it to Apple in 2020.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>133<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> 
</p><p>The CNBC article also stated Apple said no to repeated attempts to make Bing the default search engine on its devices. 
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Adult_content">Adult content</h2></div>
<p>Bing censors results for "adult" search terms for some regions, including India, People's Republic of China, Germany and Arab countries<sup id="cite&#95;ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>134<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (July 2023)">failed verification</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> where required by local laws.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>135<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> However, Bing allows users to change their country or region preference to somewhere without restrictions,  such as the United States, United Kingdom or Republic of Ireland.
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Safesearch_bing_force.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Safesearch_bing_force.png/250px-Safesearch_bing_force.png" decoding="async" width="250" height="48" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Safesearch_bing_force.png/500px-Safesearch_bing_force.png 1.5x" data-file-width="595" data-file-height="114" /></a><figcaption>Notice reading "Your country or region requires a strict Bing SafeSearch setting, which filters out results that might return adult content. If you're seeing adult content, tell us about it so we can filter it in the future. To learn more about SafeSearch requirements in your country or region, see How Bing delivers search results."</figcaption></figure>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Criticism">Criticism</h2></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Censorship_in_China">Censorship in China</h3></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Internet_censorship_in_China" title="Internet censorship in China">Internet censorship in China</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chinese_censorship_abroad" title="Chinese censorship abroad">Chinese censorship abroad</a></div>
<p>Microsoft has been criticized for censoring Bing search results to queries made in <a href="/wiki/Simplified_Chinese_characters" title="Simplified Chinese characters">simplified Chinese characters</a> which are used in <a href="/wiki/Mainland_China" title="Mainland China">mainland China</a>. This is done to comply with the censorship requirements of the <a href="/wiki/Government_in_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Government in China">government in China</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>136<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Microsoft has not indicated a willingness to stop censoring search results in simplified Chinese characters in the wake of Google's decision to do so.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>137<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> All simplified Chinese searches in Bing are censored regardless of the user's country.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>138<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>139<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The English-language search results of Bing in China has been skewed to show more content from state-run media like <a href="/wiki/Xinhua_News_Agency" title="Xinhua News Agency">Xinhua News Agency</a> and <i><a href="/wiki/China_Daily" title="China Daily">China Daily</a></i>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>140<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> On 23 January 2019, Bing was blocked in China.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>141<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> According to a source quoted by <i><a href="/wiki/The_Financial_Times" class="mw-redirect" title="The Financial Times">The Financial Times</a></i>, the order was from the Chinese government to block Bing for "illegal content".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>142<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> On 24 January, Bing was accessible again in China.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>143<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> 
</p><p>Around 4 June 2021, the anniversary of the <a href="/wiki/1989_Tiananmen_Square_protests_and_massacre" title="1989 Tiananmen Square protests and massacre">1989 Tiananmen Square protests and massacre</a>, Bing blocked image and video search results for the English term "<a href="/wiki/Tank_Man" title="Tank Man">Tank Man</a>" in the US, UK, France, Germany, Singapore, Switzerland, and other countries. Microsoft responded that "This is due to an accidental human error".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>144<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>145<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> According to an investigation by <i><a href="/wiki/Bloomberg_Businessweek" title="Bloomberg Businessweek">Bloomberg Businessweek</a></i>, the full explanation was that Microsoft accidentally applied its Chinese blacklist globally.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>146<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In December 2021, it was required by a "relevant government agency" to suspend its auto-suggest function in China for 30 days.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>147<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The search engine became partially unavailable in mainland China from 16 December until its resumption on 18 December 2021.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>148<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>149<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> According to the company, a government agency in March 2022 required that it suspend auto-suggest function in China for seven days; Bing did not specify the reason.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>150<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In May 2022, a report released by the <a href="/wiki/Citizen_Lab" title="Citizen Lab">Citizen Lab</a> of the University of Toronto found that Bing's autosuggestion system censored the names of <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Communist_Party" title="Chinese Communist Party">Chinese Communist Party</a> leaders, dissidents, and other persons considered politically sensitive in China in both Chinese and English, not only in China but also in the United States and Canada.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>151<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>152<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In April 2023, <a href="/wiki/Citizen_Lab" title="Citizen Lab">Citizen Lab</a> reported that Bing was more censorious in China than native Chinese search engines.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>153<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>154<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Copyright-infringing_content">Copyright-infringing content</h3></div>
<p>On February 20, 2017, Bing agreed to a voluntary United Kingdom code of practice obligating it to demote links to copyright-infringing content in its search results.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-bbcnews-googlebingdeprecate&#95;156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbcnews-googlebingdeprecate-156"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>155<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-guardian-copyrightcensor&#95;157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian-copyrightcensor-157"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>156<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Performance_issues">Performance issues</h3></div>
<p>Bing was criticized in 2010 for being slower to index websites than Google. It was also criticized for not indexing some websites at all.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>157<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>158<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Alleged_copying_of_Google_results">Alleged copying of Google results</h3></div>
<p>Bing has been criticized by competitor Google for utilizing user input via Internet Explorer, the Bing Toolbar, or <a href="/wiki/Suggested_Sites" class="mw-redirect" title="Suggested Sites">Suggested Sites</a>, to add results to Bing. After discovering in October 2010 that Bing appeared to be imitating Google's auto-correct results for a misspelling, despite not actually fixing the spelling of the term, Google set up a <a href="/wiki/Honeypot_(computing)" title="Honeypot (computing)">honeypot</a>, configuring the Google search engine to return specific unrelated results for 100 nonsensical queries such as <i>hiybbprqag</i>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>159<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Over the next couple of weeks, Google engineers entered the search term into Google, while using Microsoft Internet Explorer, with the Bing Toolbar installed and the optional Suggested Sites enabled. In 9 out of the 100 queries, Bing later started returning the same results as Google, despite the only apparent connection between the result and search term being that Google's results connected the two.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-googleblogbingcopying&#95;161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-googleblogbingcopying-161"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>160<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-bingcopying&#95;162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bingcopying-162"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>161<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Microsoft's response to this issue, coming from a company spokesperson, was: "We do not copy Google's results." Bing's Vice President, Harry Shum, later reiterated that the search result data Google claimed that Bing copied had in fact come from Bing's very own users. Shum wrote that "we use over 1,000 different signals and features in our ranking algorithm. A small piece of that is clickstream data we get from some of our customers, who opt into sharing anonymous data as they navigate the web in order to help us improve the experience for all users."
<sup id="cite&#95;ref-googlebingsearchresults&#95;163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-googlebingsearchresults-163"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>162<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
Microsoft stated that Bing was not intended to be a duplicate of any existing search engines.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-bingsearchquality&#95;164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bingsearchquality-164"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>163<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Child_pornography">Child pornography</h3></div>
<p>A study released in 2019 of Bing Image search showed that it both freely offered up images that had been tagged as illegal <a href="/wiki/Child_pornography" title="Child pornography">child pornography</a> in national databases, as well as automatically suggesting via its auto-completion feature queries related to child pornography. This easy accessibility was considered particularly surprising since Microsoft pioneered <a href="/wiki/PhotoDNA" title="PhotoDNA">PhotoDNA</a>, the main technology used for tracking images reported as originating from child pornography.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>164<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Additionally, some arrested child pornographers reported using Bing as their main search engine for new content.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>165<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Microsoft vowed to fix the problem and assign additional staff to combat the issue after the report was released.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Privacy">Privacy</h3></div>
<p>In 2022, France imposed a €60&#160;million fine on Microsoft for privacy law violations using Bing cookies that prevented users from rejecting those cookies.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>166<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>167<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>168<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Malware">Malware</h3></div>
<p>In 2024, <a href="/wiki/Malware" title="Malware">malware</a> was found in the official Bing Wallpaper app that tries to change the users' browser settings in order to  set the default web browser to Microsoft Edge. It has also been found stealing Edge, Chrome, and Firefox cookies.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>169<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
